Aviation and Wireless Communication 25

Wang Zhitao

Our country's aviation industry is still in its infancy. In recent years, China National Aviation Corporation's aircraft have been carrying passengers and cargo between Shanghai and Hankou, which is a rudimentary model of the aviation industry. Since the establishment of this company, its business has been developing well, and passengers also find it convenient. It can be seen that our country has a vast territory, and water and land transportation in various places are not yet very convenient. In terms of the needs of modern transportation, developing the aviation industry is currently one of the most important things for our country. That is, in terms of developing other commerce, industry, education, people's intelligence, and eliminating internal troubles and enhancing international status, etc., all of these can be promoted through the development of the aviation industry.

Since the reform in our country, internal strife has been frequent, and we are surrounded by strong neighbors. Recently, since the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident in the Northeast and Shanghai, etc., we have received extremely serious and painful lessons. All those with blood and spirit take washing away the shame and strengthening the country as the main goal, and aviation construction is the most important of all. The public is even more enthusiastic about advocating it. Therefore, the China Aviation Construction Association was established in response to the times, and the aviation industry has begun to see a glimmer of light. This is what we should all celebrate. I hope that the people of the whole country will unite and work hard to complete this great undertaking. As the saying goes, "Many a little makes a mickle," and "Unity is strength." Hopefully, foreign aggression and domestic troubles can be eliminated immediately. I hope that my comrades will work hard on this, and there is great hope for the future of aviation. In building the aviation industry, the first priority is cultivating talent, followed by perfecting aircraft and other equipment. From my humble point of view, anyone with aviation knowledge must have considerable wireless communication knowledge. No matter how perfect other equipment is, wireless communication equipment is indispensable. This is what we should pay close attention to. The ability of aircraft to fly to various places, carrying passengers and cargo, is like people having hands and feet to do things and walk. The meaning is the same. However, when an aircraft is flying and suddenly encounters heavy fog, and the direction is not clear, it can safely reach its destination without danger only by relying on wireless communication. This wireless communication device is the eyes of the aircraft. During flight, it reports the weather in various places it passes to various land stations, to serve as a reference for later aircraft, avoiding dangerous areas. This function of wireless communication equipment is the communication center of the aircraft. Being able to listen to all kinds of news from various places in the air at any time also relies solely on wireless communication equipment. This wireless communication equipment is the ears of the aircraft. Now, in Europe and the United States, the aviation industry has become extremely developed and safe. All passenger and cargo aircraft, large and small, are equipped with wireless communication equipment. Therefore, no matter how bad the weather is or how difficult the navigation is, the function of wireless communication can be used to avoid danger and seek good fortune at any time, reduce the degree of danger, and increase safety and efficiency. Therefore, it is said that wireless communication equipment has a close relationship with the aviation industry and is the most important and indispensable equipment.

Recently, I read a wireless communication magazine that had a record about aviation and wireless communication. I will excerpt the main points below for our reference, which I believe those who care about the aviation industry will be happy to hear.

Before passenger and cargo aircraft take off, they have already received reports on the weather conditions at various stations along the route. If there is no great danger, they can proceed without worry. In case of sudden changes in the weather, such as wind and rain, they can detour to avoid it. In case of fog, they can navigate blindly by following the signals emitted by the wireless beacon stations on land and reach their destination.

After takeoff, the pilot's assistant can immediately put on headphones and listen to news from various places to determine the flight direction. When the weather is clear, there are various landmarks on land during the day that can guide the route. At night, there is a beacon light every ten miles to indicate the direction. At the same time, they listen to the weather at various stations along the route and send a report every ten minutes or so to report the flight situation, location, etc., to various stations, communicating information with each other. Although people are separated by land, it is like talking face to face. Unfortunately, when heavy fog descends, so that even the pilot cannot see the end of the aircraft's wings, the pilot has already learned about the impending fog and prepared everything. Therefore, they can immediately use wireless communication equipment to follow the signals from various radio beacon stations and proceed. Upon reaching the destination, they can obtain notification from the station and land safely. The usefulness of wireless communication equipment in aviation can be seen from this. Taking the aviation industry in the United States as an example, the national air routes are densely covered, like a spider web. According to a survey in the spring of 1931, land stations are equipped with 49 wireless communication beacon stations, from which one can listen to the signals and navigate in the correct direction. There are also 21 wireless communication beacon stations available for observation to meet needs, and more are still under construction.

Wireless communication equipment suitable for aviation can be divided into two types, A and B. Type A is installed on aircraft, and type B is used in stations. Each type is further divided into transmitting, receiving, long-wave, and short-wave.

The wireless communication equipment used on aircraft is very light and small, with a power of about 50 watts, and can also be used for speaking. The radio waves emitted can range from 20 meters to 50 meters. All receivers and transmitters are made with crystal tubes to ensure the accuracy of the wavelength.

The power source is either from a wind-powered generator or from a storage battery-powered generator. All wires are properly connected, so there is no danger of damage or loosening. For cruising aircraft, longer radio waves are used, from 200 meters to 450 meters. The wireless communication equipment installed on aircraft is placed in a place that does not interfere with piloting, and with appropriate equipment, it is protected from vibration and damage. Each aircraft is equipped with a land radio station chart placed on the right side of the seat, specifically for aviation communication, so that it can respond at any time. The perfection of the equipment and the convenience of its use can serve as a reference for our country's aviation construction.

It has been found that in European and American countries, the development rate of the aviation industry is growing by leaps and bounds, and the public's confidence is also increasing day by day. Safety and convenience are widely praised. After carefully examining the reasons for the safety of navigation, although the machinery is sophisticated and the talent is experienced, the wireless communication equipment has also contributed to this perfect development. From my humble point of view, in aviation construction, we should pay close attention to wireless communication equipment, because the safety of navigation and the speed of development are closely related to it. I wonder if my readers agree?

Local News

Anniversary of the National Crisis Today 27

Solemn Commemoration Meeting

The Entire City Lowers Flags to Half-Mast and Observes Silence to Express Grief

Government Offices and Schools Operate and Hold Classes as Usual

The Chinese-Controlled Areas of the Concession are Under Special and Strict Guard

Today marks the "Anniversary of the September 18th National Crisis." The Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Citizens' Association have jointly announced that all merchants and residents should lower flags to half-mast to express grief and cease entertainment activities to show mourning. All sectors will hold a commemoration meeting at the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Corps at 9:00 AM. All party members, civil servants, military police from various government offices, schools, factories, and households will cease work for five minutes at 11:00 AM to solemnly swear to avenge the national humiliation. The Municipal Party Headquarters has issued a proclamation to the public, and the entire city has declared a state of special martial law.

Commemoration Meeting by All Sectors

Entertainment Suspended The preparatory committee for the Shanghai All Sectors September 18th National Crisis Commemoration Meeting yesterday sent a letter to the following cinemas: Cathay, Fuan, Universal, Guangming, Southeast, Xin Guang, Guang Lu, Nanjing, Guotai, Paris, Mingxing, Huangjin, Hongkou, Zhejiang, Beijing, Zhabei, Republic, Popular, Shanxi, En Ya, Central, New Central, Donghai, Jiuxing, and Guanghua; and to the following theaters: Qitian, Sanxing, Penglai, and Tianchan; and to the following amusement parks: Great World, Small World, Immortal World, Wing On, Sincere, and Sun Sun, stating: "It has been decided that the 18th of this month marks the anniversary of the Japanese invasion and occupation of the Eastern Provinces. All cinemas and amusement parks in this city should lower flags to half-mast to express grief and suspend entertainment activities on that day to show national mourning. In addition to separate instructions, this letter is sent for your information and compliance." At the same time, a letter was also sent to various newspaper offices stating: "It has been decided that the 18th of this month marks the anniversary of the Japanese invasion and occupation of the Eastern Provinces. All cinemas and amusement parks in this city should suspend entertainment activities to show national mourning. In addition to separately informing the cinemas and amusement parks to handle this matter, this letter is sent to request your newspaper offices to suspend the publication of all kinds of performance schedules on that day."

Security at the Venue A white cloth was hung high above the entrance of the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Corps, prominently inscribed with the words "Shanghai All Sectors September 18th National Crisis Commemoration Meeting." The Garrison Headquarters relayed a request to the Municipal Government Security Office to dispatch a squad of armed police officers and the Municipal Public Security Bureau to dispatch a squad of police to provide security at the designated time. The Second District Police Station has increased the number of armed police officers to maintain order and provide protection. Participating representatives from various organizations must have official credentials to be admitted and will be issued symbols for identification.

Meeting Order (1) All stand at attention; (2) Play mournful music; (3) Sing the Party song; (4) Pay the highest respects to the Party and national flag and the portrait of the late Premier; (5) The Chairman reads the late Premier's will; (6) Observe three minutes of silence to mourn the compatriots in the Northeast who suffered misfortune; (7) The Chairman gives a report; (8) Speeches; (9) Shouting slogans; (10) Play mournful music and adjourn.

Allocation of Personnel The presidium of the meeting will be composed of five organizations: the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the General Labor Union, the Women's Relief Association, the Association of Certified Public Accountants, and the Joint Association of University Professors. Reception will be handled by organizations such as the First District Citizens' Federation, the Committee to Support the League of Nations Covenant, and the Bar Association. The National Postal Workers' Union will be responsible for maintaining order. The Garrison Headquarters will be responsible for security.

Slogans and Banners (A) Meeting Slogans: (1) September 18th is a day of national crisis commemoration; (2) Eradicate the puppet organization in the Northeast; (3) Punish the rebels in the Northeast; (4) Recover the lost territory in the Northeast; (5) Compatriots across the country, unite as one; (6) Expand the anti-Japanese movement; (7) Strictly enforce economic severance; (8) Down with Japanese imperialism; (9) Eliminate the communist bandits; (10) Long live the Republic of China. (B) Meeting Banners, such as "Punish the rebels in the Northeast and recover the lost territory" and "Everyone should not buy Japanese goods; down with Japanese imperialism," etc.

Chinese-Controlled Areas Wen Hong'en, the Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, issued an order to his subordinates to strictly implement security measures. The districts and offices in Nanshi, Zhabei, Pudong, and Huxi were ordered to implement special martial law today. All main roads will be manned by double guards. All police officers will be dispatched to patrol. Inspectors, detectives, and examiners will be fully deployed, stationed on main roads to check pedestrians, with particular attention to worker and student areas and the Shanghai-Hangzhou and Shanghai-Nanjing railway stations. At Gaochang Temple, soldiers from the Naval Department's Guard Battalion and police officers from the Gaochang Temple branch will be stationed. Guard Battalion patrol boats will patrol the Huangpu River. In Longhua, soldiers from the Garrison Headquarters will be secretly deployed as sentries to check pedestrians. Pedestrian traffic will be prohibited at night. The area near the Municipal Government will be heavily guarded by the Security Brigade.

Concession Areas All police stations in the Public Concession have been ordered to implement strict security measures and prohibit gatherings and parades. All Chinese and foreign detectives will be dispatched. Armored police vehicles will patrol. Hongkou District, being a Japanese residential area, will have additional Western, Indian, and Chinese police officers and detectives stationed and patrolling all main roads, especially around the Japanese Consulate. The area east and west of Shanghai, being worker areas, will be heavily guarded. All police stations in the French Concession will have Chinese and foreign detectives dispatched. The iron gates at the junction of the Chinese and concession areas will be temporarily closed from 1:00 AM today, with only small doors on the sidewalks left open for pedestrian traffic and pedestrian checks. Armored police vehicles will patrol. Traffic at the junction is bound to be disrupted as a result.

Order to Operate as Usual

Government Notice Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Notice No. 3802, regarding the notice: "It has been decided that the anniversary of the September 18th National Crisis is approaching, and all commemoration methods have been decided by the 35th Standing Committee of the Central Committee. On that day, the entire country will suspend entertainment activities. All party members, civil servants, military police, government offices, schools, factories, shops, and households should cease work for five minutes at 11:00 AM, stand up and solemnly swear to avenge the national humiliation, and express deep mourning to the compatriots who died in the Northeast and Shanghai battles." This has been promulgated. It has recently been reported confidentially that the Communist Party intends to hold anti-Japanese movements, parades, and demonstrations in various places on the anniversary of the September 18th National Crisis, inciting the masses and taking the opportunity to riot. Furthermore, some Japanese ronin are lurking in various ports along the river, hoping to take the opportunity to cause trouble. In addition to strict precautions, this notice is issued to all industries, both labor and management, in this city to abide by the central government's regulations for commemoration, and not to participate in any gatherings to avoid being exploited. Please be respectful and comply with this notice. September 17th, 21st year of the Republic of China, Director Wu Xingya."

Operate as Usual The Municipal Government, upon receiving orders from the central government, yesterday instructed all its affiliated agencies that all civil servants should operate as usual on the anniversary of the September 18th National Crisis. At 11:00 AM, work will be suspended for five minutes to stand up and solemnly swear to avenge the national humiliation and express deep mourning to the martyred compatriots. Furthermore, the Municipal Bureau of Education, upon receiving orders from the Municipal Government, notified all schools to hold commemoration meetings on campus on September 18th to lecture on the facts of national humiliation and not to go out to parade to avoid accidents.

Radio Broadcasts Mournful Sounds

Local academic experts will give lectures on the September 18th issue at the Ningbo Road China East Company broadcasting station. The program is as follows: starting at 10:00 AM, Chen Binhe will speak on "The Origin and Development of the September 18th Incident"; starting at 12:00 noon, Xu Zuoxue will speak on "How to Commemorate the September 18th Incident"; starting at 8:00 PM, Du Chongyuan will speak on "The Chinese Volunteer Army and the Future of China."

Aviation Construction Association 28

Yesterday Held a Propaganda Meeting

Today Holds a Lecture

On the 17th morning, melancholy clouds were deeply locked, followed by autumn rain and autumn winds, shrouding this Shanghai, filled with national crisis grief and indignation. However, amid this bleak wind and bitter rain, patriotic women did not lose heart but still participated in the China Aviation Construction Propaganda Meeting held at the Sichuan Road Youth Association. In its exhibition section, there was a real airplane manufactured by the Naval Department's Aviation Office, as well as its various parts and various small-sized airplanes. There were also hundreds of photographs of airplanes used by various countries, along with various valuable statistical charts. Five to six hundred people visited continuously. Various special issues and regulations were distributed at the exhibition site. At 4:00 PM, the opening ceremony was held. Chairman Yan Zhifang delivered the opening address, followed by Yin Zhiling's report on the association's affairs. Over six hundred guests were present and were received by Huang Jing, Yao Shoukang, Jiang Junyi, Luo Yinguo, and others. Chairman Yan Zhifang began by explaining the reasons for the establishment of the association and the significance of the urgent need for airplanes. Yin Zhiling then spoke about the association's history and the reason why previous aviation organizations had failed to develop

Wang Kai Photo Studio Took Pictures 29

I

The reason was that they were either biased toward the government or too narrow-minded among experts. The Aviation Construction Association takes the national public as its main body and seeks contributions in an open manner, striving to create things for the public with the power of the public. Huang Shaohong, Minister of Transportation, was originally scheduled to attend the meeting at 4:00 PM to deliver a speech. However, he was unable to attend due to important matters and sent Director Lin as his representative to speak. The general idea was that China lacks airplanes today, and even more lacks the manufacture of airplane engines. He greatly agreed with the association's educational plan. After Director Lin's speech, Wen Tiao, the representative of the Shanghai Garrison Commander, spoke, encouraging the public to work hard and participate in the aviation movement. Li Cishan then spoke, hoping that the use of airplanes in the future would be like the cars on the streets today. He hoped that the government would open up airplanes, allowing the public to have the freedom of airplanes, and then aviation could develop. Furthermore, just as there are too many criminals in cities today, the government only knows to send them to prison, where many people share a room and gain more criminal experience and knowledge. Once they are released from prison, they do even worse. It would be better to send them to remote open spaces by airplane, allowing them to make a living on their own, which would be more appropriate. Feng Shaoshan then spoke, saying that he had been away from Shanghai for a while and that recalling the bombing of Zhabei was deeply painful. In previous years, Zhang Huichang and others flew from Guangzhou to Shanghai, and various organizations warmly welcomed them. If everyone had paid attention and implemented it at that time, Chinese aviation would not still be so immature. He visited Guangxi last month, and Guangxi's national defense is now very tight. It has over a thousand miles of border with neighboring countries. He heard that the Vietnamese side recently manufactured three hundred airplanes. The Japanese used more than two hundred airplanes to deal with Shanghai, and we already felt deeply wounded. What would happen if they used three hundred airplanes against our people now? Everyone should work hard. Mr. Chu Huiseng arrived the latest, stating that we have suffered too much from Japanese airplanes. Today, we can only take the responsibility and work hard. Everyone should donate money to build airplanes so that we can relieve the national crisis. The lecture began at 8:00 PM that evening, with Zhu Lin, a design committee member of the association, giving a general explanation of aviation and showing slides. The audience was very enthusiastic. The association's lecture this afternoon will begin at 3:00 PM. The speakers will be Zeng Yijing, speaking on "The Experience of Manufacturing Airplanes in China," Qian Changzuo, speaking on "The Future Aviation National Defense Plan," and Zhang Wenzu, speaking on "Anti-Aircraft Guns." The tickets were in great demand and were not enough. In order to accommodate more listeners, it has been decided that seating will be on a first-come, first-served basis.

Meyer's Telegram to Bode 30

No Transfer of Customs Affairs

National News Agency reports that Robert Maze, Inspector General of Customs, recently received a telegram from Bode, the British Deputy Commissioner of Customs at Dalian, stating that Fukumoto had sent him an official letter stating that he had been formally appointed as the Commissioner of Customs at Dalian and that he (Bode) should separate from Dalian Customs and hand over all keys and files to him. Inspector General Maze immediately telegraphed Bode, instructing him that his duties should not be subject to orders from outside the customs authorities and that he could not hand over the keys and files.

The Shanghai-based Central Committee members telegraphed the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government in Nanjing yesterday, stating: "To the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government in Nanjing: The Northeast has been lost for a year. The golden bowl has been missing for a long time, and the whole country is indignant. The violent Japanese are acting recklessly, regarding our government as nothing. They brazenly recognized the puppet state and signed an agreement this month, and they intend to continue to sign various secret agreements regarding military affairs, diplomacy, and the suppression of our country's patriotic movement. They have meticulous plans and have taken decisive measures. How can this be tolerated? How can the country stand? Yet the government is still as stagnant as before. In addition to the usual protests and applications to the League of Nations to send notes to the signatory countries of the Nine-Power Treaty, there are no good strategies for self-help. The so-called long-term resistance has not been seen to have any practical measures. The ambassador to Japan has mistakenly talked about direct negotiations. Summoning insult and hastening death, what shame is greater? Continuing to leave such a plan will deepen the national crisis. What kind of countermeasures will the government take against Japan's recognition of the puppet state? Is there any practical preparation for recovering the lost territory? Please quickly show the whole country with facts to dispel public doubts. The crisis of survival is imminent. We telegraph in grief and await a reply. Various Circles Telegraph to Request the Punishment of the Puppet State 32

Rather Than Sit and Wait for Death

It is Better to Rise Up and Fight with Blood

A Glimpse of National Psychology

The National Salvation Association's Telegram The telegram from the National People's Salvation Organizations Joint Association stated: "To the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government in Nanjing: The Northeast has been lost, and the mountains and rivers are broken. It began with the mistake of the non-resistance policy and continued with the mistake of trusting the League of Nations. Now it has evolved into the strange drama of the violent Japanese openly recognizing the puppet organization and signing the so-called Japan-Manchukuo Protocol. The concentration of Japanese warships along the Yangtze River is an even more blatant expression, and they will inevitably take another step to destroy us. The so-called long-term resistance, maintaining composure, and waiting for negotiations are all faults of you gentlemen who harm the country. The Preparatory Committee of the National People's Salvation Organizations Joint Association bows."

Jilin Self-Defense Army War Situation 33

Published in Shanghai Today

The Northeast has fallen for nearly a year. The people of the country share boundless grief and indignation on the anniversary of the September 18th National Humiliation. General Li Du specially instructed his representative, Wang Ziyao, to publish the war records of the Jilin Self-Defense Army's resistance against Japan in Shanghai today. A reporter from the Nichinichi Shimbun met with Mr. Wang at his residence yesterday. He was shown the original manuscript and gave an important speech, saying that the people of the Northeast, feeling the pain of losing their province and country, were sacrificing their homes to relieve the nation's difficulties everywhere. The people's morale is exceptionally high and can be used. The righteous army has fought bloody battles for years, and its loyalty and bravery have shocked China and foreign countries. As long as all parties can provide sufficient financial and material assistance, final success will surely belong to us. However, Russia's recent tacit approval of Japan transporting troops via the Chinese Eastern Railway is unfavorable to our side, which is a matter of great concern. He also said that when the Shanghai war broke out, Japan transferred Northeast troops to Shanghai. After the Shanghai war ended, they were transferred back to the Northeast. If the government had taken the opportunity to send troops to the Northeast during the Shanghai war, it would have been very easy to recover the territory. The opportunity was missed, resulting in a grave error. He couldn't help but feel deeply moved during the conversation. The original text of the war record is transcribed below:

January 8th, the Japanese instigated the traitorous Xi Qia's troops in Shencheng to lead two brigades of traitorous troops to attack Yushu County. Zhang Zuozhou, the brigade commander of the Northeast Infantry 10th Brigade stationed in the county, was extremely indignant that Xi Qia was willing to be a tiger's pawn. He decided to resist with all his strength. On the same day, Xing Zhanqing's brigade departed from Harbin for Yushu to assist Zhang's brigade in resisting the traitorous troops. On the 12th, Zhang and Xing's brigades came into contact with Yu's traitorous troops. Yu's troops were defeated and retreated. On the 16th, as Zhang Zuozhou and Xing Zhanqing's brigades were fiercely fighting with Yu's traitorous troops, Japanese aircraft suddenly bombed Zhang's army positions in Yushu Wuchang. Many nearby villages were destroyed. At the same time, Japanese troops from Jilin successively moved north to support the traitorous troops. On the 23rd, the troops of Feng Zhanhai, commander of the Provisional 1st Brigade, fought fiercely with Yu Shencheng's traitorous troops at Lalin Station, but unfortunately failed. On the 24th, Yu's traitorous vanguard had reached the edge of Acheng, and the main force advanced to Baicheng, 18 li away from Acheng. At that time, no less than tens of thousands of Acheng people fled to Harbin, and representatives were sent to meet with Ding Chao, the commander-in-chief of the Railway Protection Army, to request the dispatch of the Railway Protection Army to the city to maintain order. On the 25th, Li Du, the garrison commander of Yilan and commander of the 24th Brigade, heard that Yu's traitorous troops were heading north and sent troops to support Feng Zhanhai and Xing Zhanqing's troops. At 9:00 a.m. on the 26th, Li Du and Feng Zhanhai led their troops into Harbin. Li Du and Ding Chao immediately issued a joint announcement, declaring Yu Shencheng's crimes of disturbing the peace and unanimously condemning the traitors. In the afternoon, a Japanese plane scattered leaflets in Daowai, disturbing the public. General Li Du, having made up his mind to resist Japan, gathered like-minded people, united as one, and went to the national crisis together. They organized the Self-Defense Army and publicly elected Li as the commander-in-chief. Starting at 9:00 a.m. on the 27th, Feng Zhanhai's troops came into contact with the traitorous troops in the Huoyao Ku (ammunition depot) area. Li Du's army attacked from the left flank. At that time, four Japanese aircraft joined the battle, dropping bombs and firing guns. After Li Du's troops attacked from multiple directions, the traitorous troops were defeated and retreated. After Li Du recovered Harbin, the Japanese side lodged a strong protest and threatened Zhang Jinghui, demanding that the entire city of Harbin fly the Japanese flag by the 29th. Li ordered that anyone who dared to replace the Qing Tian Bai Ri (Blue Sky with a White Sun)

Page 15

flag would be dealt with by military law. Therefore, the merchants and residents of Harbin expressed great sympathy for Generals Li Du, Ding Chao, and Feng Zhanhai's troops. On the 28th, the Japanese army occupied the Kuanchengzi Station on the Chinese Eastern Railway, and three trains carrying Japanese soldiers advanced towards Harbin. On the 29th, Ding Chao, the commander-in-chief of the Railway Protection Army on the Chinese Eastern Railway, sent a telegram to domestic and foreign countries, detailing how the Japanese army occupied the station, shot railway workers, detained vehicles, and transported troops, violating the agreements, and that our side had no choice but to take self-defense measures. On the 30th, the Harbin-Changchun line of the Chinese Eastern Railway fell into the hands of the Japanese army. At that time, Li Du had led his troops south, reaching the Laoshaogou Station. He happened to encounter two armored trains fully loaded with Japanese soldiers from Changchun. They were head-on attacked by Li's troops, one armored train was overturned, and more than 600 enemies were annihilated. The morale of northern Manchuria was greatly boosted. Righteous armies from all over responded one after another, willing to listen to Li's command and vowing to save the country. At dawn on the 31st, the Japanese side used land and air forces to advance towards Harbin. Ding Chao's 3,000-strong Railway Protection Army engaged in a fierce battle with the Japanese army at Shuangchengbao, southwest of Harbin. This was followed by hand-to-hand combat, and both sides suffered heavy casualties. At that time, Xi Qia's traitorous Yu Shencheng's army concentrated in Acheng to support the enemy and contain Ding and Li's troops. Fortunately, Feng Zhanhai's troops seized a regiment of traitorous equipment in Yushulinzi, which made the traitors fearful. Other troops such as Zhao Yi and Song Wenjun had also arrived, joining forces to recapture the station. Ding specially issued a declaration stating that the responsibility for the war lay with the Japanese side. Commander-in-chief Li Du, Commander-in-chief of the Chinese Eastern Railway Protection Army Ding Chao, Frontline Commander-in-chief Wang Zhiyou, Chief of Staff Yang Yaojun, 22nd Brigade Commander Zhao Yi, 25th Brigade Commander Ma Xianzhang, 26th Brigade Commander Song Wenjun, 29th Brigade Commander Wang Ruihua, Provisional 1st Brigade Commander Feng Zhanhai, Cavalry Brigade Commander Gong Changhai, Yao Dianchen, Regiment Commander Chen Decai, and more than 30 others sent a telegram declaring their purpose of defending the country and the people, announcing it to China and foreign countries. On February 1st, after the establishment of the Jilin Self-Defense Army, the Jilin Public Security Maintenance Association was also established in terms of political affairs, with Ding Chao publicly elected as the chairman. Honjo informed Li and Ding that the Soviet Russian government did not object to the Japanese army using the Dongtie (Chinese Eastern Railway) to transport troops. On the 2nd, a large Japanese army arrived in the suburbs of Harbin, preparing for a general offensive. At that time, the troops under Ding and Li's command numbered about 14,000, deployed on both sides of Harbin, making a final stand. On the 4th, at around 8:00 a.m., two Japanese reconnaissance planes came to Harbin to scatter leaflets. At 3:00 p.m., four fighter planes came again, flying low over the governor's office and other places to show their power, and strafed artillery positions with machine guns. At the same time, they attacked Wujia Station with tanks carrying four steel cannons and 2,000 infantrymen. Commander-in-chief Li personally supervised the team's resistance. Gunfire and artillery fire were heard in the city, and stray bullets landed on the freight station. At dusk, the Japanese army retreated to the southwest. At 5:00 p.m., the Japanese Domon Division had arrived in the suburbs of Harbin. On the morning of the 5th, the enemy's land and air forces launched a fierce attack on Ding Chao's troops. The artillery fire was extremely fierce, and they finally broke through Ding's army positions. At 2:30 p.m., their left-wing troops occupied Daowai in Harbin. At 4:00 p.m., they entered Harbin and set up their headquarters on Xinshi Street. Ding and Li led their troops to retreat to the Binxian Bayan area, waiting for an opportunity to counterattack. On the 8th, Li, the commander-in-chief of the Jilin Self-Defense Army, issued a telegram reporting the retreat from Harbin to Binxian and stated that the general headquarters had been set up in Binxian to try to recover the lost territory. On the 19th, the Japanese army sent bomber planes, reconnaissance planes, and fighter planes to bomb Ding's army in Bayan, causing heavy damage. On the 20th, Japanese planes flew to the vicinity of Binxian again and fought with the Self-Defense Army. After being countered by our army, the Japanese planes fled. The Jilin puppet governor's office convened a political meeting, designating representatives from various counties to fabricate public opinion. The Self-Defense Army occupied 12 counties, including Yilan, and issued a telegram stating that they would never recognize the puppet regime. In addition, the Self-Defense Army occupied Wuzhuhe and annihilated the local Xi Qia's traitorous troops. On the 27th, the Self-Defense Army controlled the section from Yimianpo to Suifenhe on the Hasui Line. On March 2nd, the vanguard troops of the Self-Defense Army, led by Gong Changhai, advanced to the Laoshantou area of Harbin. Harbin was in chaos, and the Japanese army urgently dispatched reinforcements. On the 3rd, Xi Qia's traitorous troops attacked Binxian. On the 5th, the Japanese Hamamoto Regiment attacked Yimianpo, and the Amano Brigade set off for Ning'an. Wang Delin's Self-Defense Army fought bravely, but eventually withdrew due to lack of ammunition. The Self-Defense Army in the Binxian area fought fiercely with the traitorous troops for two days and nights. Because the traitorous troops were supported by the Japanese army, they occupied Binxian. Commander-in-chief Li was still in the suburbs, leading troops in a fierce battle with the Japanese army for two hours. Due to being outnumbered, he had to retreat to Fangzheng. On the 6th and 7th, Wang Delin and Liu Wankui's troops attacked the Japanese army in Ning'an and Hailin separately. On the 8th, the Japanese army in Hailin was defeated and suffered countless casualties. The Japanese army retreated to Ning'an City. On the 12th, the Self-Defense Army attacked Yimianpo. The area from Yimianpo to Hengdaohezi fell into the hands of the Self-Defense Army again. On the 16th, the Self-Defense Army advanced to Shitouhezi, 60 li away from Harbin, and engaged in a fierce battle with the Japanese army for two hours. On the 19th, Commander-in-chief Ding led his troops to attack Harbin. On the 20th, Commander-in-chief Ding led his troops back to Fangzheng to concentrate, meeting with Commander-in-chief Li. On the 25th, the Self-Defense Army captured Bincheng twice. On the 27th, Gong Changhai's troops of the Self-Defense Army engaged in a fierce battle with the Japanese army at Laoshantou. Feng Zhanhai's troops fought fiercely with Xi Qia's traitorous troops and the Japanese army at Gaolimaozi near Binxian. Commander-in-chief Li personally directed the battle in the area. The Japanese troops stationed in Harbin rushed to reinforce separately. Shitouhezi was surrounded by the Self-Defense Army, and Xiachengshui was recovered. On the 28th, the Self-Defense Army recovered Nong'an. The Japanese army dispatched troops to counterattack, and Changchun was under martial law. On the 29th, the traitorous troops under Yu Shencheng, Li Wenbing, Liu Baolin, and Li Yuyi, mixed with Japanese soldiers, advanced to the Huifa Dan area west of Fangzheng and engaged in a fierce battle with the Self-Defense Army's Feng Zhanhai, Gong Changhai, Yao Dianchen, and Yang Zibin's brigades for two days and nights. As a result, Yu, Li, and other troops suffered a disastrous defeat, and most of them surrendered. On the 30th, because the Japanese army lost Nong'an and Yu's traitorous troops suffered a disastrous defeat, they urgently transferred the brigade stationed in Korea back to cooperate with the Amano and Hasebe brigades and various traitorous troops to attack Nong'an. On April 1st, the Japanese army launched a general offensive on Nong'an. Xi Qia and the Jilin Railway Garrison were on the right wing, attacking the east of Nong'an. The Japanese Shimizu and Kuroishi troops and the Fengtian Garrison were on the front, attacking the southeast. Zhang Haipeng was on the left wing, cooperating in attacking the southeast. A certain unit of the traitorous army attacked the north of Nong'an, adopting an encirclement formation. All the Japanese planes were dispatched to participate in the battle. The Self-Defense Army's Li Haiqing's troops concentrated their main force north of Liujianfang, taking a strategic position. The battle began, and the artillery fire was extremely fierce. On the 2nd, there were fierce battles in Dajianfang, Changanbao, Niuluotun, and other areas south of Nong'an. They fought with flesh and blood, and the Japanese army suffered extremely heavy casualties. The traitorous army counterattacked Fangzheng, Yimianpo, and Weishahe, and there were battles in all these areas. On the 3rd, the Self-Defense Army's Li Haiqing and other troops in Nong'an suffered heavy losses due to the threat of Japanese planes and the suppression of artillery fire, and the rear roads were cut off. They had no choice but to retreat to Fuyu. On the 4th, the Japanese army entered Nong'an again, and Yu Shencheng's various traitorous troops counterattacked Fangzheng and fought fiercely at Gaolimaozi. Yu's troops retreated towards Binxian, and Feng Zhanhai's army tracked and pursued them. Most of Yu's troops surrendered. Li Wenbing's traitorous army was defeated by Gong Changhai, and more than half were captured. Wang Delin's troops, in conjunction with the militia, attacked Yanji. At the same time, Wang divided a part of his troops to capture Ning'an. On the 5th, the Japanese army, because Yu's traitorous troops failed to attack Fangzheng, used planes, heavy artillery, and tanks to launch a fierce attack on Fangzheng. The key points were all destroyed, and the Japanese army approached the city. The Self-Defense Army fought back in close combat. Japanese planes dropped hundreds of bombs into the city, and fires broke out in various streets. The Japanese army, together with Yu's traitorous troops, launched a siege from all directions. The Self-Defense Army was attacked on all sides and had no choice but to make a general retreat, with most of them withdrawing to Yilan. On the 6th, the Northeast rebels recognized the land lease rights of foreigners, stipulating a lease term of 30 years. On the 7th, Japanese planes bombed Yilan, and many civilian houses were destroyed, but they were repelled by anti-aircraft guns. Wang Delin's troops occupied the four counties of Yanji, Hunchun, Wangqing, and Helong. The National Crisis Conference held a review meeting and sent a telegram of condolences to Generals Li Du and Ding Chao. On the 11th, the remnants of the Hasui Line were cleared, and the war focused on Yanji and Hunchun. On the 12th, Chairman Ma Zhanshan sent a telegram to Commander-in-chief Li, saying that he had arrived in Heihe to cooperate in the offensive. On the 13th, a Japanese military train derailed in the suburbs of Harbin, killing and wounding more than a hundred people. On the 14th, the Self-Defense Army recovered Weishahe. On the 15th, the Self-Defense Army captured Fangzheng. On the 17th, the area between Yimianpo and Suifenhe came under the control of the Self-Defense Army. On the 25th, the Japanese army in Harbin moved east, planning to attack Yilan. The Self-Defense Army held the strategic points to block them. On the 26th, the Japanese Murakami Brigade attacked Shitouhezi and was surrounded by the Self-Defense Army, suffering heavy casualties. On the 27th, three Japanese mixed brigades set off for eastern Jilin. On the 28th, the Japanese army occupied Hailin, and the Self-Defense Army recovered Fuyu. On the 29th, the Self-Defense Army and Ma Zhanshan jointly attacked Harbin. On the 30th, Wang Delin counterattacked from Hailun. The Japanese army could not resist and retreated to the Wuji Mihe River. On May 2nd, the Japanese army at the Wumi River was defeated and retreated to Harbin. On the 3rd, the Self-Defense Army recovered Zhuhe and Binxian. On the 4th, the Japanese army went straight down the Mudanjiang River and attacked Yilan. The Self-Defense Army resisted fiercely. Soon, Yu Shencheng and other traitorous troops also joined the co-attack. The artillery fire was continuous, and the losses were too heavy. They had no choice but to abandon Yilan. On the 7th, the Self-Defense Army divided into two routes to approach Harbin. On the 11th, Japan transferred the 14th Division in Shanghai to the Northeast. A total of one division was transferred. On the 14th, the Japanese 3rd and 4th Divisions continued to arrive in the Northeast. On the 15th, the Self-Defense Army approached east Harbin, and Harbin was shaken. On the 16th, the Self-Defense Army fought fiercely with the Japanese between Yilan and Zhuhe. On the 23rd, Honjo arrived in Harbin by plane, planning to launch a general attack on our army. On the 24th, the Self-Defense Army fought fiercely with the Japanese army in east Harbin and blew up the Mudanjiang Bridge. On the 26th, the Japanese army, with Harbin as the center, ordered a general attack on all sides. The Japanese army on all fronts totaled 79,000, a quarter of whom were withdrawn from Shanghai. On June 4th, the Self-Defense Army's plainclothes team attacked Harbin. On the 12th, the Self-Defense Army captured Binxian and attacked Harbin. On the 13th, there was a fierce battle in Harbin. On the 14th, the Jilin-Heilongjiang armies jointly attacked, approaching within 15 li of Harbin. On the 24th, Yanji and Yushu were recovered. On the 26th, the Self-Defense Army captured Taolaizhao Zhang Weitun. On the 28th, the Self-Defense Army's Feng Zhanhai and Gong Changhai's troops approached the Jilin provincial capital. The Japanese army urgently reinforced. On July 1st, the National Government specially appointed Li Du as the acting deputy commander of the Northeast Defense Army stationed in Jilin, Ding Chao as the acting chairman of the Jilin Provincial Government, Feng Zhanhai as the Harbin-Suifenhe Garrison Commander, and Wang Delin as the Ning'an Garrison Commander. On the 5th, all routes made progress. On the 10th, the Self-Defense Army's Lu Chengcai's troops attacked to 30 li south of Yilan and engaged in a fierce battle. On the 26th, there were fierce battles at Yimianpo, Weishahe, and Shitouchingzi. The Japanese army suffered heavy casualties. There were no major changes in the Self-Defense Army stationed in various places. On September 2nd, the Self-Defense Army's Feng Zhanhai, Gong Changhai, and Yao Dianchen's troops marched towards Jilin Provincial City. On the 6th, Gong Changhai's vanguard troops had advanced to Huanxi Ridge, west of Jilin City. The rebels in the city fled one after another. Wang Delin's troops advanced to the vicinity of Changchun, and the puppet capital was shaken. Japanese Military Authorities 34

Implement Special Martial Law

Joint Announcement to Japanese Residents

Do Not Go Out for Three Days

The Japanese residents in Shanghai originally planned to hold a so-called "Invasion of Manchuria Commemoration" celebration at Hongkou Park at 2:00 p.m. today. However, the Japanese military and political authorities, in view of the high morale of our people and fearing the recurrence of a grenade incident, repeatedly jointly advised the Japanese residents to stop the gathering. Although the Japanese residents expressed their acceptance, they still intended to hold celebrations separately in their respective locations. However, Japanese Naval Commander Sakonji and Marine Corps Commander Sugita issued emergency orders yesterday, implementing special martial law in the areas where Japanese residents lived, implementing checks on pedestrians, and also strongly preventing Japanese residents from going out. The various news items are recorded separately below:

Implement Special Martial Law Today is the anniversary of the September 18th National Humiliation. The Japanese military and political authorities stationed in Shanghai, in view of the high morale of our people, urgently ordered the subordinate troops to implement special martial law at 3:00 p.m. yesterday. All the naval marines went ashore and were densely deployed in the Japanese residential area along North Sichuan Road in Hongkou, and the number of patrolmen was increased from eight to fourteen, patrolling every half an hour. At the same time, machine gun teams and armored vehicle teams were also ordered to patrol. The Japanese police force was responsible for protecting Japanese merchants and factories, and also implemented strict inspections on Chinese people passing through the Japanese residential area.

Announcement by the Japanese Military Commander The Japanese Naval Commander Sakonji and Marine Corps Commander Sugita jointly issued an urgent announcement to the Japanese residents yesterday, saying, "Regarding the urgent announcement, today is the September 18th Memorial Day. The Chinese people attach great importance to this festival, and the people's morale is extremely high. The commander is responsible for the safety of the Japanese residents and should strengthen the protection of the safety of our people. However, the scope of protection is limited to the areas where our people live. Therefore, we jointly announce that all residents must not go out freely from today until the 21st, or go beyond the scope of protection of this commander. Otherwise, if an accident occurs, they will be responsible for their own actions. This commander will not be responsible. We hereby solemnly announce."

After Japan Recognizes the Puppet Organization 35

It Will Complete Its Manchuria-Mongolia Policy

Talks with Guests from Outside the Pass

The Guowen News Agency reported that the Japanese imperialists, defying the world's condemnation and destroying the universally recognized Nine-Power Treaty, officially announced their recognition of the Manchurian puppet government they had created single-handedly on the 15th, regardless of everything. The Japanese, using the old trick of destroying Korea, sent their plenipotentiary envoy, in the style of the resident-general who destroyed Korea, who immediately signed various treasonous treaties with the puppet organization upon entering the eastern province. From then on, the three eastern provinces no longer belong to us, and the 30 million compatriots outside the pass are the slaves of the enemy's iron hooves, just like Korea and Taiwan. Yesterday, a gentleman who returned from the eastern province told the reporter in a friendly manner that Japan's ambition after recognizing the puppet organization was very detailed. I am recording it to promote the awakening of the people at home and abroad.

Complete Manchuria-Mongolia For decades, Japan has been painstakingly planning and actively pursuing its Manchuria-Mongolia policy. After the three northeastern provinces fell into the hands of the Japanese army, they first used shameless rebellious traitors and villains to establish the so-called Manchurian government, and on the other hand, they coveted Mongolia very much. Looking at the recent publication of absurd declarations, the word "Mongolia" must be written under the word "Manchuria." Therefore, the Manchuria-Mongolia policy is now the only task of the Japanese in invading China.

Attack Rehe in October After the Japanese completed the first step of their so-called new lifeline by recognizing Manchuria, they will inevitably attack the Rehe issue in the near future. One is to complete Manchuria-Mongolia, and the other is to cut off the news between inside and outside the pass to cover the world's ears and eyes. According to recent observations of the situation, the Japanese side is scheduled to send troops to attack Rehe in October. From the Japanese army's point of view, it will definitely be able to obtain Rehe without any problems.

Manipulate Finance Since Japan seized the Northeast on September 18 last year, it has spared no effort to manipulate finance. On the one hand, it urgently resumes financial businesses such as the Bianye Bank and the Three Eastern Provinces Official Bank, and establishes another puppet central bank to unify the currency system of the three eastern provinces, manipulate the business of various banks, and collect the banknotes issued by various banks in the three provinces by the central bank. The bank issues banknotes to enforce the passage of the three provinces. According to the Japanese plan, the finances of the three provinces can be completely straightened out in two years. The Japanese ambition to manipulate the finances of the three eastern provinces can also be seen.

Train Manchurian Soldiers Mr. said that the newspapers at home and abroad reported a few days ago.

The puppet military and political department of the puppet "Manchukuo" is sorting out the policy of 130,000 troops of the "Manchukuo" army, which is scheduled to be divided into three phases, but there is something unfinished. Now, no matter where the provincial fortresses are outside the pass, they are guarded by Japanese soldiers. According to recent statistics, there are more than 80,000 Japanese troops in Manchuria, while the so-called "Manchukuo" army is only about 40,000. According to reliable news a few days ago, Japan decided to instigate the puppet military department to recruit 300,000 troops, divided into 20 divisions. In addition to the original reorganization, all guns and equipment are supplied by the Japanese side, and the training period is set at two years. This plan can be implemented next spring.

Launch a Large-Scale Invasion of China Two years later, Japan's finances in the eastern provinces can be consolidated, and the so-called 300,000 Manchurian soldiers trained can be used to attack us. What is most shocking to our people is that the puppet Puyi will carry out a further absurd undertaking at this time, that is, to announce the reasons and process of his abdication, the reasons for organizing the puppet country, and to publish a statement of reinstatement. At this time, if any party comes out to resist, Puyi will immediately send troops to invade. American Ships Will Gather in Shanghai on a Regular Basis 36

Someone Threw a Bomb at Fu Xiang Ji 37

At about 12:00 noon yesterday, a young man in a western suit, about twenty years old, suddenly came to the Fu Xiang Ji yarn and thread general store at No. 71 to 73, opposite the big clock on the road of the French Concession. He walked into the store door and immediately claimed to be a member of the Red Blood Assassination Corps. Because he found out that your store was buying and selling Japanese goods, he came here to offer a bomb. He immediately took out a round bomb, as big as a ball, and threw it into the store hall, but it did not explode. However, everyone in the store was pale and had no way to escape. Municipal Party Headquarters Eighth Congress 38

The Eighth Congress of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters Opened Yesterday

Accepted Petitions from Sanyou Factory Workers in the Morning

Elected Full Executive and Supervisory Committee Members in the Afternoon

The Eighth Congress of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters was held yesterday morning in the auditorium of the Municipal Party Headquarters. Attendees included Central Representatives Wu Tiecheng, Election Supervisor Wu Jiayou, Propaganda Inspector Peng Erkang, Representative Zhong Huan from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, and many others. The meeting commenced with music at 9:00 AM. Elections were held in the afternoon. Details are as follows:

Nomination of Presidium: After the opening music, Secretary-General Tong Xingbai reported that 62 representatives had registered, exceeding the legal quorum of two-thirds. According to organizational regulations, the presidium should consist of five members. The Executive Committee had already nominated two members, Pan Gongzhan and Wang Yansong. The remaining three members were to be nominated by the Congress. Wu Kaixian, Jiang Huaishu, and Tao Baichuan were immediately nominated. Wang Yansong resigned due to illness and Chen Junyi was nominated by the Congress to replace him.

Opening Address by the Chairman (abridged)

Instructional Address by the Central Representative (abridged)

Report by Mayor Wu of the Municipal Government: Mayor Wu briefly stated that the work of the Municipal Government and its affiliated bureaus in the 20th year was detailed in the work report and would not be repeated. He would present a report to the Congress on the two most important parts of the overall work: the revival of Shanghai's prosperity and the preparation for local self-government.

Report by Representative Zhong Huan of the Garrison Headquarters: Zhong Huan reported on the pre-January 28th garrison arrangements, the course of the battle, and the general work after the battle. His speech was passionate and moving. The chairman led all representatives to stand and observe three minutes of silence in mourning for the fallen soldiers.

Petition by Workers of the Sanyou Factory: Around 11:00 AM, while the meeting was in session, Sanyou factory workers, represented by Leng Shimou and five others, came to petition. The Sanyou Company's management had violated the arbitration ruling of the Municipal Government by stopping the provision of meal allowances, leaving over a thousand workers destitute and facing starvation. They requested the Congress to provide relief. The Congress appointed the presidium and the secretary-general to receive them. In addition to fully accepting the principles, the Municipal Government was ordered to summon the management and order them to fulfill the arbitration ruling. All representatives expressed satisfaction before leaving.

Nomination of Various Review Committees: According to the regulations of the Congress, various specialized committees should be established. The chairman solicited the opinions of the representatives and decided to nominate Tao Baichuan, Tong Xingbai, Wu Xiu as well as Zhang Xiaotong, Chen Bai, Huang Xianggu as the Drafting Committee for Resolutions; Wu Xiu, Cai Hongtian, Zhang Zaibo as the Drafting Committee for Party Affairs Reports; Pan Gongzhan, Du Gang, Lu Jingshi as the Drafting Committee for Municipal Government Report Resolutions; Jiang Huaishu, Chen Junyi, Zhou Feicheng as the Drafting Committee for Garrison Report Resolutions.

Election Results: The meeting resumed at 2:00 PM. After the chairman's report, Central Election Supervisor Wu Jiayou explained the key points of the election regulations in detail. Voting then began, with the following results: The elected Executive Committee members were: Pan Gongzhan, Cai Hongtian, Jiang Huaishu, Tao Baichuan, Chen Junyi, Tong Xingbai, Lu Jingshi, Wu Xingya, Lin Meiyan, and nine others. The alternate Executive Committee members were: Huang Zaoxiong, Hu Xingyao, Long Tiyao, Xing Wan, Wang Manyun, and five others. The elected Supervisory Committee members were: Wu Kaixian, Wu Xiu, Yu Hongjun, Wang Yansong, Jiang Hao, and five others. The alternate Supervisory Committee members were: Zhang Zaibo, Zhang Xiaotong, and two others.

Details of the Completion of the Liuhekou Seawall 41

The completion of the seawall project at various sections of Liuhekou has been reported in this newspaper. The following is the full text of the report submitted yesterday to the Jiangnan Seawall Post-Disaster Committee by Qiu Xijue, Director of the Changtai Section of the Jiangnan Seawall Engineering Office: Respectfully, upon inspection, the post-disaster construction of the Changtai Section of the seawall has been completed as scheduled. A telegram has been sent to request the dispatch of personnel for inspection. According to the resolutions of your committee, the post-disaster construction of each section includes 113.2 feet of the main engineering work of two rows of three stones south of the阅兵台 reviewing platform, 130 feet of the cement wall of the 道堂廟 Daotang Temple to the north and south, 80 feet north and south of Yanglinkou, 50 feet east of Xuliujingkou, and the extension of the main engineering work includes 15 feet south of the阅兵台 reviewing platform, 7 feet south of the cement wall of the 道堂廟 Daotang Temple, 5 feet south of Yanglinkou, and 3 feet west of Xuliujingkou, for a total of 403.2 feet, as well as the repair of the stone beach slope of the 道堂廟 Daotang Temple cement wall section, and the addition of 92 feet of subsidiary embankments, and the construction of a total of 12 feet of cast stone walls for the north and south headlands, and the repair of 105 feet of the stone beach slope of the Fangjiayan cement wall section. All military destruction, including the repair of 370 feet of old桩石 pile stones, and the filling of trenches and artillery holes, and other projects, have been actively carried out since the start of construction in June. After careful consideration of the dangerous conditions on the ground and assessing the surplus of materials and labor, adjustments and additions were made to several projects. The additions include extending the main engineering work by 1.9 feet south of the阅兵台 reviewing platform, adding a row of second-layer 丈八桐 zhangbatong tung wood piles 23.5 feet long to the south main engineering work of the 道堂廟 Daotang Temple due to the particularly low beach surface, adding a row of one-row-of-piles-of-stones engineering work 6 feet long at the gap behind the south headland main engineering work of the cement wall, adding 2.5 feet of stone beach slope to the Fangjiayan cement wall section, 10 feet of the old桩石 pile stone second beach slope, and organizing 42.5 feet of the first layer, 48 feet of the outer stone slope of the cement wall section, and adding a row of sparse pile nailed plank engineering work 10 feet long at the west gap of Xuliujingkou, and repairing the old pile stone engineering work, including 8 feet at the Taojia mouth angle, 24 feet at the north pier of the阅兵台 reviewing platform, and using 100 originally stored麻袋 hemp sacks to organize a total of 930 feet of the seawall surface of each section. In addition, the first layer stones of the old stone sections of each main engineering work were widened by half a foot according to the standard drawings, and the two-foot wall slope stones were widened by one foot, and the three- or four-foot stones were raised by one foot, and the two-foot stones were used, and two to four more square feet were砌砌built per foot, and the earthen embankments were also raised and thickened separately, and one more square foot of turf was planted per foot, and all were completed by the 10th of this month. The construction time was very urgent, and it was during the hot summer and autumn floods, and the hardships and dangers were experienced. Thanks to the earnest instructions of your committee and the courageous efforts of the staff, the great project was completed on schedule. In addition to reporting the completion of the post-disaster construction of each section to the Construction Department and waiting for the completion of the detailed table, a letter will be sent to your committee for review and filing. Respectfully, this is addressed to the Jiangnan Seawall Post-Disaster Committee, Qiu Xijue, Director of the Jiangnan Seawall Daitai Section Engineering Office.

An American Woman 42

Protests Additional Telephone Charges

Jester's Opinion

Yesterday, an American woman, signing as "An American Woman" (一美人), sent a letter to the North China Daily News, stating that the Shanghai Telephone Company's increase in telephone charges had been approved by the Public Concession's Municipal Council and the French Concession's Board of Directors. There seems to be no way to oppose it publicly. However, in my opinion, it seems resistible that the company is seeking to recover the increased fees retroactively. The company provides telephone service to users based on a certain contract. If users do not want to pay the fees, they can choose not to use the telephone. However, now the company not only wants to increase telephone charges from a certain date but also wants to retroactively collect past telephone charges together. If a user's check does not match the company's bill and includes the increased past telephone charges, it will be returned by the company with a notice stating that it cannot be accepted. The company intends that if the retroactively charged telephone fees are not paid immediately, service will be suspended. I believe that there is more than just me who thinks that this should be taken up with the US Consul General in Shanghai. Therefore, I especially suggest that users can jointly refuse to pay the retroactively increased telephone fees. If the company is determined to suspend service, then they can jointly take legal action, etc.

Explosion of Industrial Raw Materials 43

Worker Flies to the Third Floor

Falls Down and Dies Tragically with Brain Matter Splattered

Two Other Workers Severely Injured

丨Police Rigorously Investigate the Cause of the Accident丨

Yesterday afternoon, a tragic explosion of industrial raw materials occurred in the Pu'an Lane of Xin Yong'an Street in the French Concession. Two people were seriously injured, and another was blasted to the third floor, then fell down, dying with brain matter splattered. Details are recorded below.

Industrial Raw Materials Company: The Hua Feng Industrial Materials Company, located at No. 5, Pu'an Lane, No. 63 Xin Yong'an Street, French Concession, is established by Cantonese merchants. It specializes in various industrial raw materials and has been in business for nearly ten years. The manager is Lin Dafu from Zhejiang, 30 years old. The chairman of the board is Xie Lilin from Guangdong. Another branch is located in Laoximen, in the Chinese area.

Huge Explosion Sound: At around 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon, a huge explosion suddenly occurred in the company's courtyard, shaking the surrounding area. Not long after, an ambulance from the Haige Road Red Cross Hospital arrived and carried away three people who looked like young workers. They were covered in blood and unbearable to look at. At the same time, the French police, upon hearing the news, dispatched detectives to investigate. They saw that most of the glass windows in the house were shattered. In the courtyard, there were two sturdy empty steel barrels, about four feet high and two feet in diameter. The top of one barrel had been blown open, while the other had not been opened.

Cause of the Steel Barrel Explosion: According to the company's staff, they had purchased two steel barrels from somewhere in Pudong a few days ago, intending to fill them with ammonia raw materials.

Lin (from Shaoxing, 28 years old), Yang Guojun (local, 26 years old), and rickshaw puller Li A'er (from Jiangbei, 30 years old), and two others opened a silver dollar-sized opening in the middle of the barrel. Unexpectedly, the lid was difficult to pry open due to rust. Yang Guojun then used kerosene to burn the lid open and ordered Wang Jinlin to stand on the barrel. As soon as it caught fire, the empty barrel suddenly exploded.

Blasted to the Third Floor: With a loud boom, Yang and Li fell to the ground at the same time. The unfortunate Wang Jinlin was blasted to the third floor, then fell to the ground, shattering his brain. Li A'er suffered severe injuries to his waist, legs, face, and other parts, and his life is feared to be in danger. Only Yang Guojun suffered minor injuries and is not in danger of death, etc. However, according to the results of the police investigation, the stated reasons are not very sufficient. If the barrel did not contain explosives, it would not have exploded for no reason. Therefore, a thorough investigation is still needed.

Sulfur Odor on the Corpse: Wang Jinlin, who was seriously injured, died en route while being transported by ambulance. The Red Cross notified the police, who then instructed the Tongren Fuyuan funeral home to send a hearse to transport the body to the morgue, awaiting examination by the Second Special District Court today. The reporter personally saw Wang's corpse, wearing a white cloth shirt and pants, a black short jacket, a white silk waistband, black socks, and black leather shoes. He was bald, and a bullet had entered from his left eye socket, piercing his occipital bone. He had a pair of glasses and several copper coins in his pocket. A felt hat was left beside him. There was no information about his family. The body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan morgue, awaiting examination by the Second Special District Court today. The reporter personally saw Wang's corpse. He was wearing a white cloth shirt and pants, with a black short jacket, a white silk waistband, black socks, and black leather shoes. He was bald and barefoot. His face was blasted black, and his facial features were almost unrecognizable. His left thumb was severed. The scene was unbearable to witness, and his body was still full of the smell of sulfur.

Sanyou Factory Workers Again on Hunger Strike Yesterday 46

After the management of the Sanyou Factory in Yinxing Port, Hudong, stopped providing meal allowances, it caused panic among all workers. Yesterday, the Seventh District Cotton Textile Industry Union still sent representatives to the Social Affairs Bureau to collect funds, and sent representatives to the Municipal Party Headquarters to petition the Eighth Municipal Congress. The workers staying at the Shanghai Hospital have continued their hunger strike. The details are recorded below:

Meal Allowances Still Not Received: At 10:00 AM yesterday, six representatives from the Seventh District Cotton Textile Industry Union, including Xia Zhongzhao, Qin Haiyan, Qin Changgeng, Bao Boyi, Wu Renfu, and Zhang Tingliang, went to the Social Affairs Bureau to collect meal allowances. They were received by Xu Yefu, Chief of the Third Section of the Bureau, who stated that the authorities would adopt effective measures to resolve the issue of worker meal allowances and were confident that they would be able to collect the funds soon and that there would be no further delays.

Workers Continue Hunger Strike: Hong Jiaben and eighteen others declared a continuation of their hunger strike at the Labor Hospital yesterday morning. They also sent a letter to Dean Fan of the hospital. Upon learning of this, Fan personally comforted and urged them to eat, but the workers were determined and politely refused. The hospital has reported to the Party and government authorities to request instructions. In addition, six workers staying at the Shanghai Hospital, including Li Hongde, Yang Xiutang, Huang Lizhong, You Junqing, Zhu Jinsheng, and Ni A'hai, upon learning of the hunger strike of their fellow workers at the Labor Hospital, also declared a unanimous hunger strike yesterday morning. The situation is very tragic, and the hospital doctors and nurses all sighed.

Worker Commits Suicide and Dies: Cai Xiqing, a sewing department worker at the factory, was 31 years old and from Jiaxing. He had a wife and five children, and their livelihood depended entirely on his work. Since the January 28th Incident, the factory announced a shutdown, and he lost his livelihood. He sent his family back to his hometown and returned to Shanghai. Because the factory still had no intention of resuming work, and he still had to support his family, he had no choice but to ask a friend to introduce him as a temporary worker at the Times Store in Nanshi, hoping that the factory would resume work. However, months passed, and there was still no hope of resuming work. Recently, he received a letter from his family requesting living expenses. Feeling his dire circumstances, he became pessimistic and attempted suicide. On the night of the 15th of this month (the Mid-Autumn Festival), he locked himself in his room and lay down alone. His colleagues in the store did not suspect anything. It was not until the day before yesterday (the 16th) that he was discovered, having taken poison. His brother, Zhiqing, immediately took him to Renji Hospital for emergency treatment, but the poisoning was too severe, and he died yesterday afternoon at around 4:00 PM.

Water Patrol Team on 47

Land Dispute on Jiangshun Steamer Reported Separately

No Police Officers Fired Shots, No Japanese Military Interference

Letter: The Water Patrol Headquarters sent a letter to this newspaper, stating, Respectfully, in the local news column of your newspaper on the 17th of this month, there was an article stating that Water Patrol police officers fired shots on the Jiangshun steamer due to confiscating two packages of soil, which led to the Japanese Navy boarding the ship and interfering with the water police. After reading it, I was very surprised. This case occurred at around 9:00 PM on the 13th of this month. Several detectives confiscated nine packages of opium soil (not two packages) on the Jiangshun steamer and sent them to the team for investigation. At that time, no police officers fired shots, and no Japanese Navy came to interfere. The information in your newspaper is inconsistent with the facts. Here is a copy of the original text of the report submitted to the Public Security Bureau regarding this case. Please correct it immediately. Sincerely, the Water Patrol Headquarters of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, September 17. Attached is a copy of the original report submitted by this team to the Public Security Bureau.

Report: The Water Patrol Headquarters reported to the Director of the Bureau, stating that at 9:50 PM on the 13th of this month, detectives Wu Chengxian and Shen Hexun reported that they saw a sampan parked outside the Jiangshun steamer at the Jinliyuan Pier, unloading a burlap sack. The behavior was suspicious. When they were about to confiscate it, people from the steamer suddenly hoisted the unloaded burlap sack back onto the ship. They did not have time to report back to the team and dispatched police officers to assist in the arrest. They chased the people to the ship's boiler room, where twenty or thirty people who looked like boiler room workers closed them in the room, surrounded them, and beat them. Detective Wu Chengxian's head was broken, and his handgun, number 11358, was taken away. Later, they captured Xu Caiyun from among the assailants and brought Xu Caiyun and the remaining small burlap sack of opium soil on the sampan back to the team, reporting for verification and seizure. Patrol Officer Pan Xiutong was dispatched, leading police chief Zhang Kefeng and police officers Bian Chunlin, Liu Jinfu, Xue Jinzhong, Sun Guozhong, Liu Jinshan, Xu Jinfu, and Song Deyun, etc., to the ship. They brought three stokers from the ship's boiler room back to the team for verification. Upon questioning, Xu Caiyun and the stokers Qian Jiting, Qian Genfa, and Zhu A'bao all gave evasive and untruthful answers. The case involves opium smuggling and assaulting public officials. They should be presented together with the witnesses and a medical certificate. Respectfully presented to the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. Attached is a list of those presented: Xu Caiyun, 37 years old, from Ningbo, is the third boss on the Jiangshun steamer. Qian Jiting, 32 years old, Qian Genfa, 28 years old, Zhu A'bao, 38 years old, all from Ningbo, are stokers on the Jiangshun steamer. Evidence: One small burlap sack of opium soil, containing nine packages, weighing a total of 550 taels, and one medical certificate.

Frugal Sales at Samsung Factory 48

Offering Profits to Aid Northeastern Refugees

Samsung Cotton and Iron Factory sent a letter to this newspaper, which begins as follows: "To the Editor, Greetings. Humanity should have a shared duty to help each other. When other countries are in trouble, aid should be given, let alone to our own compatriots. Our company, on this occasion of the September 18th National Humiliation Anniversary, is saddened by the loss of our territory and pained by the suffering of the refugees. Therefore, in addition to a one-tenth contribution from the salaries of all employees this month to provide relief, we will also allocate one-tenth of the revenue from our frugal retail sales from September 18th to 22nd to aid the Northeastern refugees. Our company is willing to sacrifice these five days' profits to help the refugees, but the amount raised during these five days, whether large or small, depends on the enthusiasm of our customers. We specially request your esteemed editor to vigorously promote this, and hope that our compatriots in Shanghai, who are well-fed and warmly clothed, will not forget the hunger and cold suffered by our Northeastern compatriots who have been displaced from their homes. We hope they will come and enthusiastically purchase our goods, which will not only alleviate the suffering of the Northeastern refugees but also obtain inexpensive, high-quality domestic products and prevent the outflow of China's interests. This is truly a single act with three benefits. Furthermore, our company is currently striving to increase production of the new 'Big Star' products to resist foreign goods. During this period of great frugality, we are making efforts to promote our products, even at the cost of sacrifice. On this day of the National Humiliation Anniversary, we must do our utmost to support the Northeastern refugees by taking the lead. We sincerely hope that our fellow domestic manufacturers will follow suit and jointly provide relief, so that more funds can be raised. Perhaps, by gathering individual efforts, we can achieve great things, and by accumulating grains of sand, we can build a tower. Our company will kowtow three times and bow nine times to thank our Northeastern compatriots. Sincerely, Samsung Cotton and Iron Factory Co., Ltd."

Doctors 51

Registration Slips Should Bear Revenue Stamps

Xu Zhicheng, Director of the Jiangsu Shangbao Revenue Stamp Bureau, sent a letter yesterday to various medical organizations, which begins as follows: "Greetings. Our bureau is now under the provincial bureau's order to urge and supervise tax collection with stricter assessments. All business documents that should bear revenue stamps but have not been stamped should be strictly enforced to increase tax revenue. Most formally licensed medical practitioners in our country are patriotic and enthusiastic individuals. When providing consultations to patients and collecting fees, the registration slips used are a type of monetary receipt. According to Article 2, Category 1, Item 13 of the Revenue Stamp Regulations, stamps should be affixed at the rate of one cent for amounts of one yuan or more but less than ten yuan, and two cents for amounts of ten yuan or more. Amounts less than one yuan are exempt from stamping. This will legalize the business documents and fulfill the obligation to respect national taxes. Your esteemed association is a legal entity in the medical community and understands the overall situation. We hereby inform you and request you to assist in notifying all medical practitioners to affix revenue stamps to registration slips in accordance with monetary receipts starting from the 16th of this month to maintain national taxes. We hope you will vigorously promote this and respond promptly."
